		}
		
	}

10/10/2023, 4:03 pm - +91 84849 31599: public boolean isPallindrome(String s) {
		// TODO Auto-generated method stub
		
		int start = 0;
		int end = s.length() - 1; 
	
		while (start < end) {
			
			if (s.charAt(start)!= s.charAt(end)){
				return false;
			}
			
			start++;
			end--;
		}
		return true;
	}

import java.io.*;

public class KeyBoard {

	public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException {
		// TODO Auto-generated method stub
		BufferedReader br= new BufferedReader (new InputStreamReader(System.in));
		
		//Writer os=new FileWriter("KeyBoard.txt");

		}
		br.close();
		os.close();
		
		
		
         
	}

2. shell2.sh
-------------

3. Write a utility to print numbers from 1 to 5 using until loop.
3. shell3.sh
-------------
i=6
no=1
until [ $i -lt 6 ]
do
  echo $no
  i=$((i+1))
  no=$((no+1))
done

-------------

no=1

   echo $no
   no=$((no+2))
   cnt=$((cnt+1))
done


5. Accept the number from user and if the number is positive find the factorial. Give proper message.
    Write a shell utility for above problem.
5. shell5.sh
----------------
echo "Enter No ::"
read $no
if [ $no -gt 0 ]
then
  x=1
  i=1
  while [ $i -le $no ]
  do 
     x=$((x*i))
     i=$((i+1))
  done
  echo $x
else
  echo "Negative number"
fi

6. Write a utility to accept 2 numbers, m and n  from user. Utility should print all even nos starting from
    m till n. Also it should print the count of numbers.
    e.g m=5 n=15
    0/p : 6 8 10 12  14
    count : 5
6. shell6.sh
--------------
echo enter the number
read m
echo enter the number
read n
cnt=0
while [ $m -le $n ]
do
  p=$((m%2))
  if [ p -eq 0 ]
  then
    echo $m
    cnt=$((cnt+1))
  fi
  m=$((m+1))
done
echo $cnt


7. Write a utility to accept number from user and check if it is prime.
7. shell7.sh
-------------
echo "Enter the no"
read no
i=2
b=$((no-1))
flag=1
while [ $i -le $b ]
do
   p=$((no%i))
   if [ $p == 0 ]
   then
     flag=0
     break
   fi
done
if [ $flag -eq 0 ]
then
   echo Not a prime number
else 
   echo No is a prime
fi
   
8. Write a utility to delete all empty files from your directory.
8. shell8.sh
-------------
for var in $(find . - empty)
do
    rm $var;
done

9. Write a utility to move all the files of size more than 0 bytes to another directory. Make sure that 
    directory is already existing.
9. shell9.sh
--------------
for var in $(find . -type f -size +0c)
   do
     mv $var newdir/.
   done

 i=$((i+1))

04/11/2023, 10:46 pm - +91 84849 31599: <Media omitted>
04/11/2023, 10:47 pm - Varad Saluke CDAC 2: Searching: Binary search trees are commonly used for efficient searching of elements. The BST's structure allows for a binary search algorithm, which has a time complexity of O(log n) on average, making it faster than linear search algorithms.

2. Sorting: Binary search trees can be used to sort elements in an efficient manner. By performing an in-order traversal of the tree, the elements can be retrieved in sorted order.

3. Range Queries: Binary search trees can efficiently handle range queries. By performing an in-order traversal within a specified range, all elements falling within that range can be retrieved.

4. Symbol Tables: Binary search trees are often used to implement symbol tables, where each element is associated with a key. The BST's structure allows for efficient key-value pair operations, such as insertion, deletion, and retrieval.

5. Database Systems: Binary search trees are used in database systems for indexing and searching records. They provide efficient access to data based on key values.

It's worth noting that the efficiency of binary search trees depends on their balanced nature. Unbalanced trees can lead to performance degradation, so techniques like AVL trees and Red-Black trees are used to maintain balance in practice.
04/11/2023, 10:51 pm - Vaibhav Patil Cdac: Def bi phatva
04/11/2023, 10:52 pm - Varad Saluke CDAC 2: A binary search tree (BST) is a data structure that organizes elements in a hierarchical manner. It is composed of nodes, where each node contains a value and has two child nodes: a left child and a right child. The left child node contains a value smaller than the parent node, while the right child node contains a value greater than the parent node. This property allows for efficient searching, insertion, and deletion operations.

06/12/2023, 9:53 pm - +91 84849 31599: public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        String n = "1101"; 

        int decimal = function(n);
        System.out.println( n + " : " + decimal);
    }

    public static int function(String n) {
        int d = 0;
        int power = 0;

        
        for (int i = n.length() - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
            int digit = n.charAt(i) - '0'; 

            
            d += digit * Math.pow(2, power);
            power++;
        }

        return d;
    }
}

06/02/2024, 8:23 am - +91 86689 50698: #!/bin/bash

# Get the list of files and directories in the current directory
contents=$(ls)

# Loop through each item in the directory
for item in $contents; do
    echo "-----------------------"
    echo "Name: $item"
    
    # Check if the item is a file or a directory
    if [ -f "$item" ]; then
        echo "Content:"
        cat "$item"
    elif [ -d "$item" ]; then
        echo "This is a directory."
    else
        echo "Unknown type of item."
    fi
done
